<Content>Loved the Embassy Waikiki !!! My family and I had the pleasure of staying at the Embassy for 10 nights in December 2008. When we arrived in our rental car, the valet greeted us and directed us to registration. The registration staff greeted us with complimentary champagne and fruit drinks for our 2 teenagers. They upgraded us to a corner unit with ocean view after we asked for a king bed in our 1 bedroom suite. We were located on the 7th floor in the Hula tower and overlooked the pool on the 4th floor. We also had a view of the Trump Tower construction; however, it was never bothersome during our stay. The room was absolutely perfect. I had read about the complementary nightly manager鈥檚 reception and thought it would be something we would only do if we happened to be around. We missed it the first night we were there. The second night we decided to attend and were so completely impressed by the complementary snacks, cocktails, and entertainment that we made it a point to attend most every night during our stay. We especially enjoyed George the bartender鈥檚 winning smile (and delicious drinks). We also already knew about the complementary breakfast and planned to take advantage. What we didn鈥檛 realize was how incredibly awesome it would be. They provide a huge variety of hot foods 鈥?scrambled eggs, sausage links, omelets, pancakes, french toast, muffins, pastries, toast, etc., etc. Plus, plenty of fresh fruit and yogurt. I gained 5 pounds during our stay 鈥?it was that good.We didn鈥檛 mind the $25 price tag for valet since it was so convenient to pull up and hop out. We took our car out every day during our stay, sometimes a couple of times per day 鈥?the valet always asked us if we needed directions somewhere. Remember, you get free breakfast every morning and free drinks/entertainment/snacks for 2 hours every night. Valet fees were a wash as far as we were concerned.I never asked our housekeeper鈥檚 name, but she was a lovely person, and I enjoyed our brief conversations in the hall. She also did a great job of cleaning up after our family and always left us an abundance of clean towels 鈥?she knew we had 2 teenagers.Did I forget to mention the hotel sits on a street (Lewers) that has shopping and restaurants within a couple of steps and is only a block away from the beach? Convenience! We felt perfectly safe letting our teenagers run down to the shops and the beach. More shopping and restaurants were located just a couple of blocks away 鈥?easy walking distance.We were so impressed with our stay. We would highly recommend this hotel for anyone 鈥?families, couples, honeymooners, etc. If we find our way back to Oahu, we will definitely choose to stay here again.

<Author>OhioLeprechaun
<Content>Loved the Embassy Suites We were very pleased with our 5 night stay. There were ample personable staff in the receiving area to help with your luggage and to check you in. Our room was clean, attractive and very comfortable and we had a view of the beach and ocean. Our first room was a view of the street. We requested an upgrade and it was completed without question. The concierge staff were very helpful regarding tours, restaurants, and other activities. The pool was outdoors on the 4th floor. Nice pool, ample lounge chairs and a fresh towel area. There were two bars. Usually only one was open at a time. At 5:30, there is a manager's reception with fresh vegetables and snacks and nice live Hawaiian music. The breakfasts, included in the room cost, were also on the 4th floor, just beyond the pool area. There was a very ample and wide variety of choices, including some one who was preparing omelets to order. The fruit was fresh and delicious. The hotel is one block from the beach and one block from a main road that has restaurants, clothing stores, jewelry stores, convenience stores, a world market,, etc. It was lit up at night beautifully. Some areas had tiki torches lighting up their areas. The hotel was in a good neighborhood and you always felt safe. The hotel is very family friendly. There is construction of a new hotel across the street, but it was not an issue while we were there. Everyone we met was helpful, polite, and in many cases, fun. We were very pleased with the hotel and will return.

<Author>tooluser
<Content>Great place to stay I stayed here for 3 nights. It was very well kept and managed. They have good security including card-managed floor access, which unfortunately did not always work and I sometimes had to ride to several different floors before getting to my own. They also very carefully check your car for damage before accepting it into valet parking, and make you sign indicating all pre-existing damage, no matter how small -- tiny bumps, dents, and scratches included. Understandable but off-putting, I guess they have had a lot of guests who try to cheat them on that. Music on the mall below would be loud from about 5pm to 7pm each night. That's all the bad though.The room was very nice, a real suite and nicely decorated. Great view of Diamond Head from the 17th floor, though no sunset from my tower. The maid service was very good and attentive - if you left early for the day they would try to clean your room right away so you could use it in the early afternoon.The business center has several PCs you could use for looking up local attractions on the internet. The evening reception includes very tasty snacks and drinks, and live Hawaiian entertainment which changes each night. Perfect for anyone to attend, including families. Surprisingly well done.The morning breakfast is pretty good and has a large selection, though they undercook their bacon (what a shame!). The made-to-order omelets were excellent. They also offer things like miso soup and edamame to cater to their Japanese guests, though it was a fun change of pace for adventurous folks from other places too, like me.I would stay here again without hesitation, though I would probably request a room away from the Waikiki Beachwalk mall, so that I would not be disturbed by the music in the evenings.

<Author>10Sgal55
<Content>Over-rated We have just returned from the Embassy Suites, staying 6 days and 5 nights. This hotel is over-rated. Yes... the complimentary breakfast is wonderful, and the management hosted cocktail happy hour is a plus, but the hotel fell flat on other issues. We were disappointed to find that the only room they could give us was a room located right next to the ice machine and the elevator in the Aloha tower ( We booked our vacation in July, so our vacation was not a last minute decision). We offered to pay for a partial ocean view, but was told this was not available. Our room on the 17th floor over-looked the Beachwalk area and had a view of Diamond Head, so the room did have a very nice view. However...at night it was very noisy, especially when we wanted to sleep. We thought the loud music was coming from the Rum Fire (a new nightclub at the Royal Hawaiian shopping center), but we were informed the loud music was coming from the Yard House, a restaurant located below the Aloha Tower. Switching rooms was not an option, as we were told the hotel was 90% booked. Another drawback are the very uncomfortable beds--way too soft and lumpy. The mattresses look very old and dated, far older than the age of the hotel!

<Author>sunnyfaced
<Content>Honest review of Embassy Suites My husband and I went to Oahu for our honeymoon and stayed at the Embassy Suites through a hotel/air/car package and got a good rate. Embassy was clean and everyone was very nice, as most people in Hawaii are, but as a honeymoon hotel, it wasn't exactly what we had in mind. It depends what you like, but hotel seem to have a lot of families with young children. We think it is great for that purpose, especially with the free breakfast. We were fine with the average decor and offerings because we went outside the hotel a lot, for dinner, breakfast extras, etc. We like more the contemporary setting and loved the Mona Surfrider to hang out- great not having to pay to stay there- and also Halekulani and Waikiki Parc-where Nobu is located- one of the best meals we had in town. We were able to do these extras without the stress of paying too much at a hotel per night, so in that sense, Embassy was fine. It was clean, the construction wasn't the best backdrop at the pool, and sort of banal. Good rates though and good for families.

<Author>Bazza99
<Content>Embassy Suotes Stay Oct 2008 The Embassy Suites in Waikiki was great but the rooms were a little small. We had two adults and two kids in our room. It wasn't a big deal because we were always busy and spent very little time in our room! We got our room for $230./night, the location was great! Some people complained about the walkway to the beach, I just went through the two hotels in front of us with no problems. I also used their showers to get the sand off! If you can't pull that off you're a rookie!! Parking does stink at $25 per day but if you can't afford that maybe you shouldn't be vacationing in Hawaii! I also really enjoyed the Beach Walk right below the hotel, ABC store was right across the street! By the way we stayed in the Hula tower on the 10th floor. After a night of drinking the hotel key in the elevator to get to your floor was a hassle but ..........If you include the breakfast and happy hour this place is a great deal! I don't think I'll be going back to Waikiki for about another 10 years (I prefer Maui) but if I do I'll look at the Embassy Suites first and if the price is right I'm there!Also, the Trump Hotel construction next door did not bother us at all!!

<Content>Perfect for a family We stayed here for a week in early October. It was a wonderful stay and the perfect location for our family. The hotel was lovely and conveniently located between the beach and the Royal Hawaiian Mall. Breakfast was excellent, especially eating in the open air cafe. We never waited long for anything and the staff was very friendly. Housekeeping was wonderful and our suite worked out great for us: me, hubby and 2 girls ages 6 and 10. Most days we did sightseeing but were back to the hotel by around 5pm. The manager's special was nice - there is live entertainment and hula every night. The appetizers aren't anything special: veggies/dip, chips/dip, chips/salsa and open bar. However, it was very relaxing for us to head down there, enjoy the music, some snacks and the kids would swim until bedtime. It worked well for us to hang out and just order some food at the hotel by the pool. A nice way to end each day. You can walk to many locations or easily catch the bus. Two negative comments: the room was advertised to have a king bed but it only had a queen. Also, be wary of the concierge. One morning the gal introduced herself at breakfast and proceeded to tell us that our plans were all wrong, would never Other than that, I can only say good things about this place. Very family friendly, very clean and well maintained and more.

<Author>d28872
<Content>Best Hotel Ever If you want excellent service, beautiful, spacious room, and prompt service, choose to stay at Embassy Suites. My sisters and I vacationed in Waikiki from October 21 through October 29th and had wonderful service from all the Embassy Suites staff. This was my 3rd trip to Oahu, one sister's 2nd trip and the other sister's 1st trip and all of us agreed that we have never experienced better accommodations and service. When we asked for 5 towels in our room, within minutes they were provided as well as five hand towels. Our check-in (took 15 minutes at most) was seamless and the friendly, helpful staff were wonderful. One example of the excellent customer service provided was the friendly, helpful Activities coordinators (especially, Cyndi, Heidi, and Christina). They were available during breakfast and their approach was friendly and helpful without being invasive. Conversation began by asking if we were having a good time and what our planned activities were for the day. They, then, offered any help with suggestions, experiences, and offers to make registrations. We accepted their offer to make our reservations for Star of Honolulu and Polynesion Cultural Center (twi-light dinner and show). In both cases, we had great reservations (7th row for the PCC show and front table for the Star of Honolulu show). We couldn't have been happier with our stay. With 3 women sharing a room, the spaciousness of the suite was awesome and fit us perfectly. Large bathroom, two lanais, queen size beds (very comfortable), and huge rooms (both living/dining room and bedroom) made our stay an absolute joy. We will never choose any other hotel again now that we know how it feels to be pampered. There other amenities provided such as free use of the business center to check email or print boarding passes, free phone calls, and unbelieveable breakfast choices were perfect to suit all our needs. We also had an unusual request to weigh our suitcases for our return trip, and the bellhop service came through for us by providing a scale and weighing our suitcases prior to check-out. All I can say is you won't be disappointed choosing Embassy Suites as your hotel of choice.

<Content>Good Value in Honolulu The Embassy Suites in Honolulu isn't actually on Waikiki Beach, but it's close enough to provide easy access without the higher cost of those on the beach. It's a typical Embassy Suites property, with a complimentary breakfast and manager's reception above the norm. Breakfast includes excellent fresh fruit in a very nice setting. It's really a very good value for the location.

<Author>Sammk
<Content>Good location, Great time Embassy is great. From the valet parking; to the check-in where you get a glass of OJ. The valet and bell people were terrific. The service was wonderful.We had an ocean view room, 2 queen beds in a separate room with a hide-a-bed in the living room. QUIET room in the Aloha tower on the 21st (top) floor.The highlight to me was the manager's reception. I know some reviewers think this was tacky. But the food is snack food by design. They serve hamburgers, chicken fingers, nacho's for the kids etc. for a price. But, the bartenders make strong drinks. Well worth the free price. Throw a dollar or two in the tip jar and your set.. Breakfast buffet had everything you would want. Omlettes, French Toast, Pancakes, Cereal etc.The beach near the hotel (across a small side street) and down a short path is small and doesn't have many waves to bodysurf. We went down toward Kuhio Beach to get more waves and see more people. That's what you do in Waikiki anyway, people watch.Highly recommend this hotel. Walking distance to everything fun on Waikiki

<Author>Bystedt
<Content>Good location, good value Before staying at the Embassy Suites Waikiki Beach Walk hotel I read the reviews here and had very high expectations. For the most part, the hotel delivered on these expectations. I would like to highlight a few things that stood out beyond what you'll read in the other excellent reviews on this site.**THE GOOD**SPACEThe rooms/suites are very spacious and practical. This is the best feature about this hotel.CHECK-INFriendly staff at check-in with mini mocktails and a free Hawaiian CD.VALET PARKINGAlthought a little steep at $25/day, they were very friendly and efficient.LOCATIONThe hotel is surrounded by a number of excellent restaurants including Roy's and a fantastic little Italian place called Arancini. Tons of shops are also within walking distance.**THE BAD**THIN WALLSThe rooms have really thin walls and you can easily hear conversations in adjacent rooms. If you have noisy neighbors and you're a light sleeper, you might have sleep issues. HOTEL POOL BARThe Pakini bar at the pool closed at 5pm on most days we were there, which was fairly disappointing considering the excellent location and ambience at nighttime.BREAKFASTThe buffet breakfast had a cafeteria feel to it with a large open area with tables. Food was fairly basic and the selection was quite limited. For instance, there were no real options for different bread types (just bagels or toast - no rye, wholewheat, multi-grain, etc.) or cereals (no muesli) and there were no boiled eggs (hard or soft) or sandwich meats/cheeses. Having recently been to stay at a similar level of hotel in Helsinki (Finland) this was the area that really stood out as a disappointment at the Embassy Suites. The one good thing was that they had some Japanese breakfast options. OVERALL FEELThe hotel didn't have a luxurious feel to it. Doors, furniture, fittings, the shower-in-shallow-tub did have a slight mid-range hotel feel to it. Maybe I expect too much but I was hoping for a bit more of a luxury experience at this hotel. For this reason, I would not recommend this hotel to honeymooners or others who want a really special experience in Honolulu.

<Author>kiwimum2
<Content>Excellent in every way We are a family of 4 and had the pleasure of staying at the Embassy Suites. We had requested a partical ocean view room and was delighted with the room we received. Our corner suite had views directly over the pool/breakfast area and out to the sea. Being a corner suite meant we had a extra set of windows along one wall offering this great view. We loved having a seperate bedroom with 2 comfortable queen beds and a seperate living area with a very comfortable sofa bed. The breakfasts are adequate and alway replenished quickly, if I was to be very fussy I would have liked a white tablecloth on the table rather than eat off a tray! The managers reception is nightly offering an open bar from 5.30 - 7.30pm which included cocktails, spirits, wine, beer and soda, they also provide entertainment and snacks. Embassy Suites has ideal location, shops and great restaurants on the ground floor. We ate at Ruth Chris Steak House and The Yard House both meals were great and only steps to your hotel lobby. The beach is only a short walk across the road. Our room was very quite but over the weekend The Yard house at the bottom of the hotel becomes a nightclub at 10pm so we did hear some music from that but not enough to bother us. I would definately stay there again and recommend to friends and family.

<Author>TeamIguana
<Content>Perfect - except Trump Tower view We stayed here for 4 nights in early September '08. I would say everything was pretty much perfect except our partial ocean view was basically of the new Trump Tower. I suppose I should take my wrath out on Trump more than Embassy Suites. Also, by requesting a king bed in one of the two bedrooms I think I doomed my party to such a view. Requesting two queens in each room might have prevented our plight. The description of partial ocean view was actually quite accurate. If you stood away from the sliding doors about 15 feet and looked out, all you saw was the ugly grey, frame work of the Trump Tower. However, if you were on the balcony or even on the couch closer to the doors (and closed the curtains two-thirds) all you would see was the ocean and the sail boats. If you look at enough pictures you will realize this hotel is not exactly on the beach. But there is a view of the ocean between the corridors of the hotels in front and that view is pretty spectacular in itself. I hate to keep bringing up the Trump Tower but I can only imagine how wonderful a view there must have been just a year prior - because behind the Trump Tower is a government facility (meaning no high rises) which is more of a park, and behind that is just coastline and ocean. By the way, the Trump Tower construction is up to about 20 floors and I believe by the time it is done it will be over 40 floors.Enough about the view and the Trump Tower. Just go in with the expectation that there might be a bit of construction Monday through Friday and it does basically overlook the pool.Speaking of the pool, it met our needs. I can see how it might be small during the summer time when it is full of kids, but I was able to do some simple lap swimming every morning when it opened at 9am. And it has a nice shallow section for small kids. So the pool was just right.The breakfast was fine. True, it is the same food every morning but what do people expect? I find it to be a nice time saver having a breakfast buffet downstairs, not to mention it is a lot cheaper than eating out. They have a nice omlette station and a good selection of fresh fruit. And of course they have the usual selection of pastries, potatoes and bacon/sausage.The parking is a pain at $25/night. Most tourists need a car in Honolulu to get out of the city but if you are only there to see Waikiki, maybe consider shuttling in direct from the airport. There are lots of restaurants within walking distance, not to mention all the shops too. Getting to the beach required a short trek (maybe 5 minutes) from the ground floor to the public beach access outlet. The nearby beach is basically at the very end of what most know as Waikiki Beach. It was convenient for me to take my toddler. All we needed was a pile of sand and some ocean water. But I think the main beach scene was a bit farther away. Getting back to the hotel, the ammenites were satisfactory. The fitness room was open 24 hours. It seemed clean with a decent selection of a few treadmills and free weights. Most of the equipment had TV screens and there were some other screens in the corner of the rooms. It was stocked with towels, a water cooler and disposable earphone covers for the TVs. Don't expect anything huge. It was small but served its purpose.The rooms were quite well furnished. Everything seemed quite modern. The microwave and refrigerator in the room are Embassy Suite trademarks that I basically expect when I travel now. The in-room safes are large enough for a laptop and the free in-room internet connection seemed fast enough for work purposes.Housekeeping was a bit slow as some reviewers have previously mentioned. Being on the upper floors did seem to slow down the staff getting to the rooms. But they did a fine job once they got there.I would normally have given a 5 star review but that Trump Tower is so annoying. It almost would have been better to request a city view and just stared at the hotels on the other side. But it is always nice to be able to see the water, even if you have to close one of your eyes when looking out the windows just to get an unobstructed view! Other than that, this Embassy Suites was just fine!  
<Date>Oct 8, 2008

<Author>luv2travel822
<Content>Location, Location, Location We stayed here for three nights at the start of our two week vacation. We are fans of the Embassy, and it is not the first time we have stayed at one of there properties. The room was comfortable and clean, the fridge is nice to have. The hot breakfast buffet and managers evening reception are the added bonus for us. Wakiki is very expensive, and having the buffet in the morining to start your day was wonderful, and the reception in the evening to have a cocktail and snack before heading out to dinner was also wonderful. Reception snack changed daily, so that was nice and there is also nightly entertainment. Reception bartenders very friendly. The beach is one block up and there is a paved path between the Outriggar and another hotel but it is narrow and lined with rat traps (this is not maintained by Embassy) and smells like trash. When walking to the beach come out of the hotel near the front desk and turn left, cross the street and turn right there is another path to the beach that is very nice. Most of the staff was very nice, some of the front desk staff could have been more friendly and the staff member preparing the omletts was downright rude. Donald Trump has to be the biggest you know, and he is building a 20 something story hotel next door, they were on floor 22 when we were there, so the construction noise can be a bit annoying when at the pool. However, remember this is a big city and it is noisy regardless. Our view was of his building, but I did not mind, I found it quite interesting, and we could see the rest of the city also. One of the best things is you can take the escalator down from the pool/reception area on the 4th floor and you are smack dab in the beach walk area of shops and resturants, very cool.

<Content>A great hotel We just returned from 8 days at the Embassy Suites Waikiki Beachwalk and could not have had a better experience, especially with a one bedroom suite, complimentary cooked breakfast and cocktails for the rate we paid. They also changed things around, e.g. sometimes waffles, other times french toast. I loathe spending over $1 to have a pair of underpants washed!The only thing that I would recommend to the hotel is to provide a retractable drying line in the bathroom over the bathtub.The location of this hotel is great. We could get every where we wanted on foot or by car. And there is a wonderful variety of food, in all price ranges within walking distance. And great shopping! Would definitely stay here again and have been recommending it to everyone.We didn't want to leave.

<Author>cowboyTexas
<Content>Nice hotel, some disappointments This was our second stay at the Embassy Suites Beach Walk. The first stay (summer 2007) was better than our recent visit.What we like: relatively spacious rooms, new hotel, close to shopping and restaurants, close to beach, nice breakfastDislikes: 1. Trump tower construction noise is a modest annoyance during breakfast and occasionally caused stopped traffic on the only access road to the hotel2. Concierge desk (in lobby, and next to the breakfast area) will not give honest opinions and good guidance because they are actually working for themselves via kickbacks. Case in point: one concierge at breakfast tried to sell surfing lessons for $70 (and tried a pressure-sale by saying that the lessons were almost sold out), when you can actually walk-up and get lessons at multiple locations for $40).3. We had a smoker in an adjoining room, and the hotel staff would not track him down and make him stop. We had to switch rooms, and lost a view of Diamondhead and beach in the process. The manager did discount our room rate though.4. The southern tower is better than the northern tower (forgot the names of each tower). The northern tower only has 2 elevators, so you have no choice but to cram as many people in as possible, or never leave your floor!Advice: 1. select the southern tower if possible2. ask the bellhops or the valet parking staff for guidance instead of the concierge staff! Unlike the concierge, they were very helpful. The valet staff are especially nice.

<Author>xbioman
<Content>Good value, but lots of construction We had a one bedroom suite and it was nice and roomy. Decent view although the new Trump Tower being built next door has almost destroyed their view for most rooms on the West side of the hotel. The down side right now is the noise. The Trump Tower crew starts work about 7:00 AM and the Outrigger next door is also undergoing rennovation. We are not late sleepers so it was not that big a deal, but it is very noisy on the West facing rooms. If you are going now, try to get an East (Diamond Head) facing room.The breakfast buffet is good, great selection, but the atmosphere is kind of like eating at Disneyland. Crowded, noisey, not at all relaxing.Overall though, this hotel is a very nice value given the room size, friendly staff, services and location.

<Author>st0ked
<Content>Loosen up We were a little concerned that the construction noise would be too much. Not at all bad and our room looked directly at the 18th floor of Trump. There was more noise coming from the hotel across the street on the ocean side. There was an ocean view if I stood on my tip toes or hung over the lanai but the real view was the city at night. What a great place. if you're bothered by a little noise, maybe you should stay someplace other than Waikiki. Loud music, loud vacationers and FUN. We didn't know what to expect upon arival. The desk staff seemed a little snooty. (He had to put down his newspaper to help us) Due to delays, we had been traveling for quite some time and looked it. It's a nice hotel but it's an Embassy not the Waldorf. Loosen up a little bit. We were given a King in the Aloha tower. The bedroom was right next to the elevator. The sound of the cables was the first thing that we noticed. When I called the desk I was informed that all king rooms in that wing were next to the elevators. We decided to stay and I'm glad that we did. It was the view over the city and the park that won me over and I didn't really notice the elevator cables for the rest of the stay. There's plenty of great dining choices just feet from the hotel. No hotel restaurant but if you're hungry and don't want to walk the 150 feet there's good food at the pool bar.Breakfast was fine and the late afternoon entertainment was fun. Milan at the concierge desk was extremely helpful. With his guidance we were able travel the entire island without once renting a car. You haven't lived Oahu to it's fullest until you've done it by bus like the locals do. (He also knows the best places to party!)Another tip is to allow for an extra $5 a day as a tip for your maid. You paid big bucks for this vacation and that paultry $5 will be well worth it. For that extra $30 during our stay, we had the best maid service anywhere! The room was cleaned by our schedule and everything was perfect.

<Author>MochaRose
<Content>What a pleasure! My boyfriend and I stayed in a one-bedroom suite when we visited Waikiki Beach last weekend for his family reunion, and our entire stay was a treat, starting with the complimentary welcome cocktail as you check in. I found our room to be cool, clean, and comfortable, with a beautiful city view, mini fridge and microwave for our convenience, and even two flat screen TVs. The complimentary fresh cooked breakfast was wonderful every morning (the omelette station is a must), the pool was beautiful with a bar of yummy island cocktails, and the overall appearance of the hotel was lovely. The hotel is a very short walk from Waikiki Beach, and in the middle of a promenade of quality shopping, touristy shopping, and restaurants. Think Rodeo Drive, but with lit island torches. And the staff was very helpful and knowledgable of the area--they were able to make recommendations and get us transportation to wherever we needed to go, for a reasonable few dollars. The only downside was the construction of the Trump tower next door, which provided a little noise, and a not so lovely visual from the pool, and some rooms. But otherwise, I would highly recommend the Embassy Suites for an island stay experience that is truly sweet.

<Author>slub007
<Content>Good and Bad but mostly good OK. I stayed here just last week and was here for 6 days. I came with my girlfriend and chose this because it was one of the most highly rated here that was available. This is my experience while checking in...I got there and (because I'd read about the construction and also warned not to get a room next to elevators) I requested a room away from both. I was told that the only rooms with King beds was next to the elevator. I was also told that there were none with Kings away from contruction. I was given the option to pay an additional $50 per night to get a room with 2 beds on a high floor away from elevators and Trump construction. I was extremely annoyed because I felt like I was the victim of the old 'bait an switch'. It was terrible way to start a vacation. Nevertheless, i paid it because I'd rather pay more for peace than ruin my entire vacation. Once I got to the room , it had a wonderful view and the decor, etc. was nice.This is the list of pros and cons based on my experience there...Pros:Location (right in the edge of Waikiki and you can get to just about anything on the beach from here)Newness (the room was updated and modern)Staff (friendly and courteous)Business Center (Internet access..whoo hoo!)Breakfast (the breakfast buffet is probably the most memorable thing about the hotel)Managers Reception (can't go wrong with free drinks. the snacks were not that good but it WAS free)Cons:Pool (always crowded with wayyy too many kids. Can you consider an adults-only hour or two a day?? One day, a young girl threw up in the )Location (the front of the hotel is on the Trump construction side and it's a pretty small narrow street. Some tour buses are not allowed down this street because they don't fit.)Fitness room (This was small and while they DID have quite a few treadmills, it's inadequate for weighlifters)Final thoughts: If you're looking for a hotel with lots of 'stuff' then this is the wrong place for you. The Hilton Waikiki Village has shops on th epremises and a private lake, etc. It seems to be more adult friendly. I've heard that they nickel and dime you to death and it's older and tackier. If the hotel for you is one that's clean, and provides a good home base so that you can explore the island. I'd recommend the Embassy Suites.

<Author>ejm3
<Content>Construction Notwithstanding, a Nice Hotel Before I booked this place I knew 3 things from reading Trip Advisor:1) Construction noise (thanks Donald)2) Lots of kids3) It ranked #5 in Honolulu, where there are about 8 million hotelsAfter having stayed there for 6 nights, I can confirm that there is in fact construction noise, a fair amount of kids (no big deal really) and it was a clean, nice hotel in a great location for a decent price. I paid $249/night AAA rate and I didn't feel overcharged at all.A couple things to note:1) If you select a room with a king-size bed you will be next to the elevators and they will annoy you all night long. We moved to a room with two double beds and while not our first choice it was much quieter and we were happy.2) The construction noise is very real and very annoying. However, our second room was in the Aloha tower on the side away from the construction and noise was a non-issue after that. If you have a room on the side where the construction is happening it will probably bother you. Something to consider.You will not, however, be able to escape the noise while at the pool. If you wait until 3pm to visit the pool you will avoid the noise.3) I was unaware of the free breakfast when I booked the hotel and was very pleasantly surprised. The food was good and there was plenty to choose from. This is NOT the cheesy continental breakfast most US hotels offer. They also have a Manager's Reception each evening with free drinks and snacks.4) Valet parking is mandatory and costs $25/day before tips. We were able to rent a car for the day for $38 and returned it that night. That might be a better solution if you're a cheapskate like me.Overall the staff was friendly and helpful. Suite setup is great and bathroom is quite large.Location is great with plenty of shops  restaurants nearby and the beach is a 5 minute walk.The ABC Store (2 right outside the hotel) will have everything you'll need at reasonable prices. I would definitely recommend this hotel to friends and family and would not hesitate to stay here again.

<Author>DamianLittle
<Content>All the free stuff..for Hawaii.. WOW, what a nice place In the past I have been a guest at the Hilton Hawaiian Village and was very happy! As a loyal Hilton Family guest, when I saw this new Embassy Suites I jumped on the opportunity to stay here, and this is the perfect place to stay. The suite had a small counter top with a snick, microwave, and mini -frig, a nice sized sitting with with balcony, the bedroom was also a nice size. Both the bedroom and sitting room had a flat panel TV. The bathroom was what I would call basic, nothing special. A good size and clean. Here is the best part, all the free stuff. There was a nightly managers reception around the pool area, with a limited open bar, more then beer on tap, you can get all types of mixed drinks. There was also a very nice hot food buffet. The breakfast was also very nice, with a large layout.. All this is in your room rate.. but wait there is more.. FREE Internet, and PHONE calls.. You get like 100 min free phone calls anywhere in the USA. Parking was the only extra free $25.00 per day, they only offer in-and-out valet parking. It was a nice service, but I do not like to tip someone every time I want my car.. As a Hilton Diamond member I really did not notice any thing special from all the other guest. The staff was nice, but you are just a number to them. I think you get this at any big resort area hotel. I would stay here over and over.. You get a nice bang for your buck.. You can walk to the beach in 5 min, and many rooms have very nice views.. A very good family place, and I was very happy with this place.

<Author>UCDJay
<Content>Really good hotel, great value for the money I give the hotel 4 stars, and I'd add half a star after the Trump Tower construction is finished. It is a nice hotel with a friendly courteous, staff, good location, and the free amenities are a huge bonus.The Construction Issue:The noise wasn't too bad, it was noticeable but not overpowering during breakfast, and they stopped around the same time the reception began. We were in the Hula Tower and did not hear any of it from our room, even with the lanai doors open. Overall, it was noticeable but not distracting or too much of a nuisance. If you are sensitive to noise, then I would suggest staying at a different hotel.Value:The free breakfast is a great value, and it's probably save a couple 40-50 bucks a day, and even more if you are bringing a family. It was not too crowded and there was plenty of food. French Toast, Waffles, Pancakes, Eggs, Cereal, Oatmeal, Omelettes made to order, Bacon, Sausage, Fresh Fruit, Yogurt, Bread (White and Wheat), Bagels, Baked Goods, Coffee, Milk, Juice, and soda were all readily available. The food is fresh, and of decent quality. It's what you would find in a normal restaurant, not crappy cafeteria/dorm food.The manager's reception had snacks such as peanuts, chips, salsa, egg rolls, crab potstickers, cocktail sausages, salad, and other small snacks. They had well drinks, and the beer was Bud Light and Michelob Amber Bock.Staff/Service:One of our main complaints was the concierge service. They were unable to get us a rental car in Waikiki when we simply looked online and booked it ourselves through Budget. They were helpful in calling cabs and giving us shuttle information. I say book the activities on your own, but use them to get you taxis, shuttles, and other basic info. We had one housekeeper who wasn't very good, but another who was very nice and friendly, and waited till we left the room to start cleaning. Overall the staff was friendly, and accommodating, but again, book the activities yourself.Location/Facilities:The hotel is perfectly located. Its about a 1-2 minute walk to the beach, and there is plenty of shopping and restaurants all on the same block and within the area. The little Coco Cove convenience store is nice and a good way to pick up water, drinks, snacks, or other things that you don't want to walk very far to get. They also have Dole Pineapple Whip! The pool and spa area is nice, and was not very crowded. The bar is a little expensive but if you want to have a drink and relax by the pool its a nice convenience. The workout room was well equipped, but it was a bit too stuffy and hot, they definitely need more ventilation and fans. There is also free water in the workout room so if you have a refillable bottle you can just go in there and fill it up if you don't want to pay for water. The business center was very convenient, and the free printing is extremely helpful. Overall, I liked the decor, and the building was new, clean, and nice. Parking is expensive, $25 a day, so I suggest looking for parking elsewhere.I'd recommend this hotel, the free breakfast is a really nice touch and can save you a ton of money especially if you are bringing kids.

<Author>samjoco
<Content>Good location We spent a week at the Embassy Suites in a one-bedroom suite. The location is far better than most--just across the street and down a short walkway to the beach. Just down the hallway from the registration desk are several shops and fun eateries. The room was fine but a little smaller than other Embassy Suites we've stayed in. One pleasant surpise was that our city view room had a nice view of the ocean from the balcony. The courtesy breakfast was hit with the kids, offering pancakes, french toast, potatoes, omlets, scambled eggs, sausage, bacon, and breads every day. The kids loved the pool, which was very clean, with a little shallow area just right for our young ones. The hotel has a coin laundry facility, which after talking around, I found was rare for Waikiki.Our main disappointment with the hotel was the lackluster housekeeping. Several days there was still a lot of sand on the bathroom floor after cleaning. OUr kids made some big smudges on the coffee table and sliding glass door on the second day that were never removed. Overall though, it was a pleasant experience and I would recommend this hotel if you need the space offered by a suite.

<Content>Great Family Hotel! We just came home after 8 days at the Embassy Suites and had a wonderful time. We thought it was a great family hotel. We stayed in a 2 bedroom suite with our 3 children and my mother-in-law which was perfect for us. Both bedrooms and the main room had a flat screen television. The rooms were spacious and clean, and we had a partial ocean view which was nice. The construction from the Trump tower did not affect us - we never heard any construction noise as we were on the opposite side and the few times we were at the pool we didn't notice the construction noise either. We loved the area we were in - lots of great shopping, good restaurants and just a short walk to the beach. A previous review mentioned that the guests at the breakfast buffet were pushy and rude, but we didn't experience that at all. I found that everyone was very polite and people were patient and waited in line to get their food with no problems. The staff at the hotel were friendly and always helpful. We enjoyed the nightly entertainment with drinks and food in the evening the few times we were able to go. We had a pretty busy itinerary so we only went down 3 times in the 8 days we were there, but the entertainment was great and it was nice to sit down and relax with a drink before going out to dinner. We would definately stay at this hotel again and would recommend it to other families going to Waikiki.

<Author>summerfun3711
<Content>Good location, however there are some negatives... My family of 5 and my parents stayed here for two nights at the end of our trip to Hawaii. Originally, we were booked to stay at the Hilton Hawaiian Village, but were able to add a night to our vacation but not to our reservation. Hilton let me know that they had availability at Embassy Suites. Having stayed at the Suites in Maui, and having such a positive experience, I thought that this would be a great alternative and booked the reservation, letting them know that my room would need to accomodate 5 people. (3 children, two adults, which did not seem to be a problem with the person taking the reservation --although he did inform me there was a fire code in Honolulu which allowed only four people in a room.) I also booked a suite for my parents and requested that the rooms be adjoining or close to each other. My last request was that if possible I would like a late checkout as our flight did not leave until 5pm. I prepaid the reservation and all seemed good.In terms of location, the hotel was a good choice--actuallly better than the Hilton Hawaiian Village since it was closer to the shops and other action of Waikiki. A negative to the location is that there is alot of construction going on across the street at Trump's new building and also at the Outrigger across the street. Construction starts early (although not a problem for us as my children are early risers) Also, the construction had more of an impact for us staying in the Aloha tower, which directly overlooks Trump's building, so much of the view is scaffoling and cranes.Another negative was with our checkin experience. Upon checkin, the woman informed me that I had too many people booked in my room, which was against fire code and that she would let me go this time. I informed her that Hilton had directly taken my reservation and that I had been forthcoming with the number of guests which they accepted and took my prepayment in full for. She still insisted she was doing me a favor and was quite rude and condescending. The interaction was embarssing to me as other people checking in heard the exchange. It was quite an unfriendly way to be greeted and left a bad taste in my mouth from the start. Next, she informed me that there was no way that my request for adjoining rooms could be honored. She could not even offer me rooms in the same tower. When I requested to speak to a manager, he informed me that although I had requested the adjoining rooms, I had not indicated that I was traveling with others--which left me slightly confused because whey else would I have requested adjoining and and prepaid two rooms if I was not traveling with the people--and quite honestly, what is the difference in requesting an adjoining room and indicating you are traveling with someone?The next negative was our room. We were taken to room 110 in the Aloha tower. In this room, there were no lanais, so the room felt like a closet as our only view was the Trump construction through a small window--no lanais or fullbig windows to open up the room.On a positive, my parents were in room 729 in the Hula tower. Their room had an ocean view, 2 lanai's--really nice. In general, rooms were clean, spacious and rather up to date decor--contrary to another Outrigger property we had stayed at in Waikiki on another visit. The manager's reception was ok-- Food offerings included cocktail meatballs, eggrolls, sliced sub type sandwiches, fresh broccoli and cauliflower, goldfish and on another night, fried zucchini. Not a bad selection for an appetizer to hold you over until dinner. Each reception included entertainment. Breakfast had many offerings. Eggs, breakfast meats, made to order omlettes, pancakes, fresh fruit, etc. There was definitely something for everyone. The pool is on the 4th floor. It is a nice pool and has a great toddler section. Only problem, it is kind of breezy on the fourth floor (wind seems to really move between the buildings. Also, pool is right alongside Trump property under construction.Other amenities offered were free wireless internet access, complimentary first 30 minutes on each long distance call, free printing, good selection of television channels. Regarding houskeeping, although we were on the 1st floor, they did not get to our room until after 3:30, when were coming back from being at the beach all day. We had to ask them to give us 20 minutes to clean up and then leave our room again so it could be cleaned. I should also note that our last request, a late check out, was also not honored. I called the evening before checkout and they told me I could call in the am and they would let me know if they wold honor it. So I called 7am the next day, and they said no, but when my family was ready to shower/dress for the airport, it might be possible to utilize a hospitality room if one was available. When I asked if I could reserve one, they said no--it was first come first serve, however, 1pm was usually not a problem. At 1, I went to the front desk to make my request (mind you we had checked out of 110 at 11 am). At first the woman told me they did not give out hopitality rooms between 1 and 3. I told her this was a contradiction to what I had been told. She hesitated a while, went in the back and gave me a key to room 101. When I took my boys upstairs to change, it turns out that this room was in the middle of being cleaned--sheets ripped off the bed, dirty towels on the floor etc. I'm not sure what a hospitality room should offer, but at minimum I would think clean towels. Interestingly enough, I am not sure why I could not keep my room until 1:30 as housekeeping had obviously hardly started cleaning this floor. One thing to note: I had a conversation with another woman who had a family of five staying there. When I asked her what Type of room she had, she said a one room suite like my own. I asked here if she was given a hard time. She said no--she had booked through the Waikiki suites directly and they said they would let her put her family in there, although it was against code, this one time. Our last negative experience: We inadvertently left our ipod on the desk in the suite when we checked out (very careless on our part). We realized this upon checkin at the airport. We immediately called the hotel and asked them to please double check our room. Interestingly enough the ipod never turned up.

<Author>Linette705
<Content>Loved the Embassy Suites We spent 2 weeks at the Embassy Suites Beach Walk with only positive experiences to report. Our stay began with a very hospitable check in and the hospitality continued through the rest of our stay by all hotel employees we encountered. We stayed in a one-bedroom partial oceanview room. The room had a small fridge, microwave, sink, a flat screen TV in the bedroom and main room, free internet connection and 20 minutes of free long-distance calls. Included was full made to order breakfast daily and a compliementary nightly manager's cocktail reception. The breakfast is a huge buffet with something for everyone including chefs to cook eggs to suit you. The nightly managers reception included beverages, appetizers and local entertainment (of which we always enjoyed). Staff at the Conceirge desk were always helpful with booking tours or providing directions if necessary. The pool deck was kept immaculate. We were impressed to see that the rock planters and waterfall in this area were scrubbed down with brushes several times a week. Everywhere on this property was clean and well maintained. Embassy Suites is just off the beach, close to Fort DeRussy. Restaurants and shopping are plentiful in this area. Several restaurants close by offer discounts to Embassy Suite guests. Some of our favourite restaurants were the Yardhouse, an italian restaurant across the street (can't remember the name) and Senor Frogs. I would recommend this property to anyone. We paid around $300.00 per night and it was worth every penny. When we go back to Waikiki, there is no doubt in my mind that we will stay there again!!LinetteSherwood Park, Alberta

<Author>patswamber
<Content>Not all that relaxing Our family stayed at the Embassy Suites March 14-20th. We chose this hotel based on previous reviews and we actually split our vacation between 2 different properties - the HHV and here.Nothing really new or different to provide on the perks for this location: The rooms are big and the location is central - it's easy to get everywhere. Front desk and bell staff are friendly, location is excellent with lot's of restaurants, coffee and shopping nearby. All the staff at breakfast and the evening reception were wonderful, drinks were strong. They have singers and entertainment, which help to drown out construction noise during the breakfast and evening reception.However, many of the other items that other posters have listed as positives just didn't thrill me. I found it difficult to relax. Here's what I didn't like:1. Contruction noise is non-stop from both the Trump Tower and the Outrigger Reef. It's really distracting during meals and at the pool. The constant view of the construction site was also a negative.2. Behavior of guests at breakfast was absolutely zoo-ish. Think of a high school cafeteria or the early bird special at Country Buffet. Loud, crowded and pushy. The food, however, was good, nice variety of items. The evening reception was more civilized but the food wasn't as good.3. The pool was a decent size for waikiki but it was crowded with wild, unsupervised kids. No one seemed to be monitoring rough behavior while the parents drank at happy hour.4. Houskeeping never made it to our room on the 4th floor until after 4pm each day. It always seemed to coincide with us returning from the beachI know many guests have found this hotel to be wonderful for the amenities offered and it wasn't a bad stay for us. I guess I was just expecting something a little more peaceful. I will return to Waikiki but I probably won't come back here.

<Author>IowaGrandparents
<Content>Pretty Nice for Waikiki Enjoyed the first two nights of our (almost) annual Hawaiian holiday at the Embassy Suites. Good place to crash upon escape from a Midwestern winter and to get ready for a week of R  R. We even managed to arrive just in time for the manager's reception that continues until a respectable 7:30 PM with complimentary live entertainment, wonderful hors d'oeuvres, and first class beverages available. Plenty to tide us over from a day of travel until the morning.We did reserve early (6 months in advance) and paid the premium price to guarantee an oceanfront room. But it surely was quite nice to be able to sit on one balcony of our room and watch the ocean or sit on the other and watch the Trump construction that other reviewers have mentioned.Compared to many other Embassy Suites they have a very efficient breakfast setting with plenty of capacity -- and even live breakfast entertainment on one of the days we were there. No waiting and really nice inside or outside seating options. (If outside, don't leave your plate unattended to get a coffee or juice -- the birds who live in the neighboring palm trees come for breakfast too!)Keep in mind that Waikiki is an urban resort. It's sort of as if Midtown Manhattan had been relocated into the middle of the Pacific. If you want to get out of city, you need to choose a different setting (we spent the rest of our time in Kauai.) However, if Waikiki is your destination, this property is located almost exactly at mid point of the hotel row and a really easy walk from any of shops, restaurants or markets. Even Cheeseburger in Paradise is, in our opinion, an easy stroll and well worth it. The nightly street performers are just a few blocks away, but so is the widest and best sand beach on the strip. One general hint. We've found that simply taking a cab to or from the airport is by far the most convenient route to the beach hotels and, for two of us, not all that expensive comparatively speaking. Also, given what you're going to spend for your vacation anyway, it's not much of an additional investment over the hotel buses. In fact, on the way back to the airport, the bellman put us in a stretch limo whose driver was glad to charge us only the standard cab fare (about $35 at present.)  In summary, we've stayed at several places on Waikiki. This may not be our favorite but it certainly is a great place that we would highly recommend. Families would probably find it to be a dynamite setting for location and value both. As grandparents, we enjoyed just watching and listening to the numerous families who happened to be there at the same time we were. Thank you for sharing your joy with us -- unknowing though it may have been!  
<Date>Mar 25, 2008

<Author>DHerrold73
<Content>Fantastic Stay at the Embassy We just returned from a 7 night stay at the Embassy Suites in Waikiki with my three daughters - ages 9, 7  6. I'd have to say that I have an overall favorable impression of the hotel after our stay.Everyone on staff was pretty friendly and polite. Our room was clean and comfortable. We didn't have a beach view, but our room overlooked the pool area, and we had very quick access to the pool which was convenient for the kids.The breakfasts win the show in my eyes. Having full breakfasts (it's a buffet and you you can order omlette's or eggs) was big for our kids who woke up every morning pretty famished. The manager's cocktail reception is nice in that you have an opportunity to enjoy some drinks and light snacks prior to going out to dinner each evening.Location wise was OK. It's just a couple blocks to the beach which can be a long walk for our kids after a long day at the beach, but not too overhwelming. You do have immediate access to the main strip on Waikiki so you can access all of the shopping  dining very quickly.Overall a very enjoyable stay - one hotel I would visit again. It didn't completely wow me to get 5-stars, but was the perfect fit for our family vacation.One note - the consierge area that booked all of the activities were friendly, but not all that helpful. I think they had their own agenda to sell their various tour packages, so make sure you do your own homework on all of the various activites and prices.

<Author>entheos
<Content>A WONDERFUL mini "getaway" My husband and I just got back from a mini getaway 4 night stay at the Embassy Suites, Beachwalk, and enjoyed EVERY MINUTE of it! We are actually locals, and decided to book a hotel for the weekend since I am 32 weeks into my pregnancy, wanted to relax before baby comes and didn't want to fly. We have stayed at other hotels on the island before (Hilton Hawaiian Village, Ihilani, Turtle Bay and Double Tree hotel) but Embassy was by far THE BEST. We thoroughly enjoyed the full breakfast buffet every morning! Since we knew there was a mini refrigerator and micro, we brought deli meats and breads, left over pizza, fruits and drinks and packed it up for lunch and spent the afternoons at the beach right across the street. It was nice to also come back to relax by the pool, only to get MORE pupus and drinks at the manager's cocktail hour. The breakfast, our snacks and manager's cocktail hour held us over for the whole day. We didn't eat at a single restaurant our entire stay, except for going downstairs every night to get a coffee and some Beard Papa's cream puffs or Mondo Gelato (with buy 1 get one free coupons we got from the hotel) to relax and people watch. We took advantage of the many free nightly music groups at the hotel, or spent our odd hours reading the complimentary newspaper delivered to our door each morning. The hotel was extremely clean and the wait staff at the open lanai eating areas were very efficient and friendly. My husband and I plan to return each year with our new family as an easier alternative than flying away for vacation! We're HOOKED!

<Author>MikelFallCity
<Content>Excellent - Service - hotel - Everything We loved this embassy suites. It was right in the middle of everything. Just a short walk to the beach, many restraunts, shopping and people watching. We had to upgrade to a 2 bedroom suite because the fire code in Hawaii won't allow 5 people in a 1 bedroom suite, which didn't make a lot of sense but the manager made it good. We were right on the beachwalk and the activity below was fun to watch. We even had a peek a boo view, if you stuck your head off the balcony really really far.I was irritated about the valet parking fee, but in the end enjoyed not having to find a parking spot when we were coming back from a long day, and having that feature made us feel rich because we would not pay for that if it was an option. The valet attendants were great as was the reception staff. I would stay here again for sure. I would recommend the yardhouse and the holokai grill for dinner. The yardhouse has a ton of beers on tap, and a small happy hour, not many foods on the happy hour menu. the Hula grill above Dukes has a great happy hour.Something else that we did to cut costs is that Wal-Mart is very close to the hotel, we went and got those rolled mats for the beach, they were 1.39 a piece there, and we got water and munchies for the hotel room. We also bought a compact cooler, we really could have used an umbrella and I wish I had thought about it while we were at wal-mart. Try the swap meet for great souveniers, there are coupons in the oahu book at the front desk to get in.

<Content>What a great stay! We stayed at this Embassy Suites for a week. We upgraded to a full ocean view after the first two nights next to the elevator. Do NOT stay next to elevator as it is extremely noisy. The Ocean views were fabulous. Three sets of sliding glass doors, two from the living room, one from the bedroom. My husband found the Trump Tower construction fascinating to watch, although I did not quite share the sentiment.The breakfast was simply the best, fresh pineapple and papaya and other fruit every morning. The omeletts to order were very good. Indoor/outdoor breakfast area was kept very clean. Entertainment was certainly an added bonus. Nighttime reception was very worthwhile. Try the mai tai drinks. Many umbrella type drinks to choose from and the music and hula dancers were quite good.The staff was all very friendly, front desk, housekeeping and concierge. We needed to use the Bus since we did not rent a car, and the concierge was always happy to give us complete directions to get us to our sightseeing destination. You can get almost everywhere on the local bus system. We found this hotel the nicest Embassy Suites we have ever stayed at, and it was a completely enjoyable week.

<Author>momtravelingcircus
<Content>Absolutely no reason to stay anywhere else! My family of five (kids aged 7, 5, 10 mos) just got back from a five-day stay at this hotel. There are just not enough superlatives to describe how perfect this hotel was for our needs. For one, we got the 2-room suite at almost half its price by booking through NWA World Vacations. The generous breakfast buffet was perfect for us mainlanders who were awake and hungry too early in Hawaiian time. This was an awesome buffet with many many cook-to-order choices and bountiful tropical fruits too. I ate my lifetime supply of papayas and pineapples here. And there was even a ukelele performer providing live music every morning. They also have an evening reception with free cocktails and free food (egg rolls, meatballs, tuna sandwiches, etc)! How awesome is that. Kids loved it. And while you eat all the free food and swim in the pool in between, there was also an evening performance with slack guitar or ukelele music with a graceful hula dancer too. The hotel is also a block from Waikiki Beach and is adjacent to a great selection of stores (including Beard Papa, Mondo Gelato, and Teppan Sushi) so you really don't need to venture far to get a full Hawaiian experience. The hotel also gives guests a free CD of beautiful Hawaiian music. It is a special (smart) touch that transports you right back there when you are back to your ten-below-zero hometown.

<Author>wubear
<Content>Good unless you want a quiet hotel This hotel is clean and offers a lot of space for your money. But it is not a quiet hotel. I stayed on the 11th floor and had a good view above the shopping center, but the noise from the restaurants and street below came right through the sliding glass door when it was closed. The other side of the building is also where all the trucks, buses and other vehicles approach the building so it isn't much different. Plus, the new Trump hotel/condo/retail shopping is being built so the view of Ft DeRussy Park is going away. It is very close to the beach and everything else in Waikiki. Here's the downside for those who care. The front desk staff is quite unfriendly. No eye contact and very few alohas after you check in. Not even the concierge desk or bell staff cares if you are a guest or not. Especially not the valet parking staff. They all seem to get along fine, but unless you approach them to want something, they do not acknowledge your presence. I found that highly disrespectful for a hilton property. You get better service at other hiltons, such as the Kuhio Prince on the other side of Waikiki. However, the housekeeping staff and pool staff are very friendly and service oriented. They are the saving grace of the hotel. The front desk manager has a lot to learn about service and should take some lessons from the other managers.

<Author>EdnaDurango
<Content>Excellent service, above and beyond expectations We were in Maui for a wedding and decided to spend a couple of days on Oahu to see Pearl Harbor. We'd never been to Honolulu before, so we booked a suite at the Embassy Suites Waikiki Beach Walk with our Hhonors points. Since we were not regular paying guests, we did not expect to receive the wonderful service that we did. When we checked in, the staff gave us the name of a local sushi restaurant that was incredible and was right across the street , named Sushi Koh (see our other review). There was construction going on across the street and they gave us a room on the opposite side so the noise wouldn't bother us, and we didn't even have to ask for it. The staff was very friendly and helpful, the breakfast buffet was great. Hospitality hour bartenders were awesome, although the appetizers weren't so hot. Didn't really matter, when rating the whole experience! The hotel, while not right on the beach, is located on a street with lots of boutiques and restaurants, in a park-like atmosphere. Once we saw the beach scene on Waikiki, we didn't want to go to the beach anyways - it's sure not Maui, that is for SURE. The pool area was very nice, except for the construction zone overlooking it, across the street. Didn't bother us at all. We hardly noticed. Free internet service in-room and in the lobby. As a matter of fact, I am writing this review in the lobby while we wait for our airport shuttle - that's how impressed I am.On our last day on Oahu, our flight did not leave until 8:00pm. We requested a late check-out (1:00 pm), but were told it was not available for that room. However, they offered an alternative - to switch rooms that morning, and we could have that room until 1:00. We switched rooms, and left for our early morning Pearl Harbor tour, which was arranged by the Embassy Suites very competent bell staff. When 1:00 arrived, we checked out, checked our luggage, and were given a special key to the swimming pool floor so we could use the pool and services for the afternoon, including beach towels. Not only that, when it came time to get ready to leave for the airport, they let us use a hospitality suite for 1/2 hour to shower and change clothes, free of charge. We have never been offered this extra service before and we are very grateful to have had the opportunity to rinse off the chlorine and suntan lotion before going to the airport.Although Waikiki Beach is not our style, we thoroughly enjoyed our stay at Embassy Suites and were extremely impressed with the level of service we received. We would recommend this hotel to anyone planning a visit to this part of Oahu.

<Author>fhata
<Content>Great Stay at the Embassy Suites Beach Walk We always try to stay at an Embassy Suites on our vacations and the new Beach Walk Embassy did not disappoint. Located on the new Beachwalk you are just a few blocks away from the beach and main shopping on Kalakaua Ave. Kalakaua Ave reminds me of Michigan Avenue with all the shopping you could imagine. We had the most luck starting the day early, having breakfast around 7:00AM and heading out by 8:00 for our activities. The breakfast lines are small enabling you to get an omlet easily and a nice array of fruits and usual breakfast faire. Also rice and miso soup are included which was a nice touch. You have the choice of eating inside or out on the lanai on the fourth floor.The rooms are new and clean with great service by the staff. Everyone was very friendly and helpful. The manager's reception was very popular with a host of drinks to choose from and nice appetizers. It gave us all time to unwind and decide where to go for dinner.We would definitely stay there again. The location is hard to beat. If you enjoy staying at Embassy Suites, you will like the Beachwalk.

<Author>Kids3
<Content>Awesome Hotel for families This is a brand-new (rehabbed) hotel and it is great. The location was great - across the street from Waikiki Beach and adjacent to the beautiful new Beachwalk, which has restaurants and shopping. It is also just a block from Ala Moana Blvd., the main shopping street. The outdoor pool is awesome and much bigger than most Waikiki pools. The hotel is clean and nicely furnished and the rooms are spacious and comfortable (though a little smaller than other Embassy Suites properties, but this is Waikiki). The free open-air breakfast is wonderful, with many choices, high-quality food, and live entertainment. The breakfast alone will save you a bundle (and a lot of hassle) if you are traveling with family. Truly a great value for the money.

<Author>kimo767
<Content>Good for families or business trip, not peaceful We stayed for two nights on November 3-5, 2007. I realized too late that the hotel is located in the most traffic congested and noisy area of Waikiki (most of Waikiki is congested and noisy). The Embassy Suites are twin towers about a block inland from Waikiki Beach and next to beautiful Fort DeRussy Beach Park. It's just a short stroll to the beach, so no big deal. There are alot of new shops and restaurants in the revitalized Beach Walk area.The rooms are well appointed, cozy, and the service is attentive. There is a small pool on the 4th floor plaza that seemed to be filled with screaming kids and teenagers most of the time. The breakfast area is like a brightly lit, noisy, high school cafeteria with little charm. The two pool bars were also overlit with bright flourescent lighting and very uninviting. You WILL stand in line for your breakfast, your drinks, your snacks, and the elevators. If it rains, you will get wet trying to get to the cafeteria for breakfast from either tower. Everyone at the pool gets to watch and hear the new Trump Tower construction team work loudly until 2009. We also had a close up view of the construction from every window and balcony of our room, and the workers could watch us in return.Parking was an overpriced $25USD day plus tips for speedy valet service. Don't forget anything in your car, like a cell phone, as it is a hassle to retrieve later.The poorly designed open air front desk area must have been designed by the same design team who put bright flourescent lighting in the bar/pool/dining areas on the 4th floor. The sweaty staff and guests also can smell car exhaust through the humid lobby. Lobby needs to be glass enclosed and air conditioned for a quiet, relaxing environment. For a more peaceful stay, I would recommend the nearby Halekulani, Hilton Hawaiian Village Resort, Ilikai, or the Hawaii Prince Hotel on Ala Moana Blvd. You will not feel like you are on a kid-filled Disney Cruise at these properties.  
<Date>Dec 5, 2007

<Author>thetractorman
<Content>Loved it! My wife and I stayed here for a weekend between a couple of business meetings, and we loved this hotel - it's one of the nicest I've been to lately. I'd stay there again if I go back to Honolulu. The hotel is close to Waikiki Beach, but you probably can't see it. Walk across the street and between the Outrigger hotel buildings to get to the beach, which is now just a narrow strip of sand. In fact, the waves were hitting the sea walls on much of the beach. We rode from the airport on a shuttle bus, and were immediately greeted by cheerful and helpful staff. No matter what we asked about at the activities desk, they were able to help us determine what to do and how to get there. Our suite was very nice, with the expected very comfortable bedding and pillows, plus they had nice plasma TVs. Since I had already been on the road a week, we took advantage of probably the nicest hotel guest laundry room we've ever used. The evening reception and complimentary breakfasts were very nice, and the 4th floor rooftop lanai was very relaxing, although it was quite breezy one evening when a storm blew through. You can save a bunch of money by taking advantage of these complimentary foods rather than paying the expensive Hawaii prices elsewhere. There are many great places to eat nearby, but you might try either Ruth's Chris Steakhouse, or some great seafood at Roy's - both are in the Embassy Suites buildings. If you go to Roy's try the Ahi and the Butterfish!

<Author>SwanDev
<Content>Best family hotel in Waikiki We stayed at this hotel twice in August for a total of four nights and the staff provided nearly flawless service for my family and our traveling companions. We traveled with our 15 m.o. child and our friends traveled with their 10 m.o.. All-in-all this was the best hotel experience that we have had in Waikiki, where we travel annually to visit friends and family. The location is great for easy access to restaurants and shopping. And even though the Trump CondoHotel is underconstruction across the street, the construction noises never disturbed our stay on either the 4th or 9th floors.Check-in was relaxed and efficient, our rooms were in good condition with comfortable beds and plenty of room for the three of us. It was great to have the living room available for the crib and the separate bedroom for me and my wife. It is important to note that this hotel has at least two room configurations, with the bathroom accessed either from the living room or from the bedroom. You should request whichever is appropriate for your purposes upon check-in. We elected for the bath off the bedroom so that our toddler could sleep undisturbed in the living room.Breakfast was the typical Embassy Suites selection with cooked-to-order omelets and other standards. The distinction here is that they also offer Miso soup, salad and a few other Hawaiian and Japanese items like Haupia yogurt and Portugese sausage that are a nice and tasty complement to a standard American breakfast.Valet parking seemed a bit expensive at $25/day but the service was tremendous as we never waited more than a minute or two for our car. Valet and Bell Staff were plentiful, polite and quite helpful with directions and information. Also there seemed to be staff everywhere, (this is good thing) always cleaning or otherwise busy. The hotel is new and it will continue to look and feel new if the staff remain as attentive to cleaning and maintenance as they were during our stay.My only complaint, about our two stays is that upon checking in on Saturday the hotel did not have a crib available, even though we had called and requested one several weeks before our trip.. The hotel did arrange to borrow a crib from a nearby hotel , but we had to wait for an hour or so for it. Our toddler was not too happy about this after flying all day. This was not a problem on our second stay the following week.We stayed in both towers and on the 4th and 9th floors during our two stays. Depending on your interest, you may want to request a room overlooking the pool in order to listen to the nightly music from your balcony. We found the 4th floor to be particularly nice as it is the level of the breakfast and nightly cocktail hour,. After our son went to sleep in the evenings, we were able to sit out on the patio (with the baby monitor) and enjoy the music and conversation with friends, knowing that we could be back in the room in just a few seconds if he needed anything.This is a great hotel for families , but was not overrun with children. There was also an interesting mix of retirees, college kids and foreign tourists. We plan to stay here again next year.  
<Date>Sep 4, 2007

<Author>ilovethelonghorns
<Content>Great Family Hotel - We loved it! We have been to Honolulu numerous times and stayed at many different properties there. The Embassy Suites ranks right up there as one of our favorites. We had a corner unit with two balconies looking straight out to the ocean. The corner units definitely have more space-try to get one if you can. The rooms are very comfortable and clean, also surprisingly quiet. The free breakfast every morning was a treat- we love the fresh omelette station with many varieties of fillings that you get to pick out yourself and put in a bowl - also delicious fruit and mixed green salad. One morning they had a Hawaiian singer serenading us while we ate! The Happy Hour was enjoyable too. Mai-tais were pretty good, also try the Blue Hawaiian. There were different entertainers every night for Happy Hour including awesome hula dancers with island music. The pool area was nice sized and there was a great hot tub we liked usingas well. The Embassy Suites is in a perfect location. We loved being able to walk through all of the great shops along the Beachwalk and enjoyed eating at several of the restaurants adjacent to the hotel-including Roy's, theYardhouse, and the Hono Kai Grill. All of the staff that we encountered at the hotel were friendly and bent over backwards with any request. We truly think that anyone would be happy here! We did not encounter any construction noise at all on our visit but it does look like it could be a problem in the future. We feel that the Embassy Suites Honolulu delivers a relaxing, roomyalternative to travelers of all ages.

<Author>SugarWahine
<Content>All good, but you gotta love kids..... Just stayed for 4 nights. Great spot and centrally located. Nice rooms, though the Aloha tower is nicer than the Hula tower.... closer to the ocean view. The beachwalk is great with some nice new shops and some fun places to eat. The rooms are big and the pool area is quite nice (for those complaining about the size of this pool, this is a huge pool compared to other hnl pools- traditionally they are much, much smaller). The staff was quite nice and all were very helpful. Roy's was a great place for drinks and snacks and of course being across from the Halekulani is a treat. (do not miss the coconut cake!) A few quirks: 1) this is a huge family hotel. You gotta love kids and not be bothered by them running amok. One afternoon there were 40 plus kids in the pool..... (yes, I counted) 2) breakfast is great, but unfortunately there are quite a few vultures (aka guests) there so be ready to fight for the food. People think nothing of taking 25 slices of papaya for themselves.... or taking as much as they can carry away after eating their breakfast. kinda gross. I know its expensive to have a family stay in hnl, but come on now.... it was a bit extreme. I can imagine that ES will have to crack down on this eventually..... 3) There is a ton of construction going on around the hotel, so if you are sensitive to that, beware. It did not bother me, but we spent most of the day away from the hotel.4) The hotel parking staff warned us to beware of the HPD that hang out at the stop sign behind the Trump construction, this is the only way to drive away from the ES. Come to a full and complete stop at that stop sign..... they come out on foot from behind the construction and pull you over if you do not do this, even though the construction makes it very difficult to see. Better safe than sorry.

<Author>LisaGoldCoast
<Content>Wahoo Waikiki We stayed at Embassy Suites recently during a work conference (yes, a conference is Hawaii), and loved it, the location is great with just a short stroll to the beach and located right amongst the new Waikiki Beach Walk.
