<Author>Miller5
<Content>Fabulous-life is good We stayed at the Embassy for nine days and it was 10 times better than I ever imagined it would be. I had read every review prior to going and felt like I knew what to expect.Arrival: We were greeted in the open air lobby by very friendly staff; thanks Jaymar. We didn't smell any fumes at any time that we were in the lobby area. We were given juice and champagne cocktails to enjoy while we checked in. Our room wasn't ready yet, so they gave us a changing room on the first floor. The room was beautiful but smaller than the one we resevered, as I found out later.POOL: The pool was large in size and it was nice to have the wading pool attached. We didn't hear any noise from Trump even though construction was going on most days we were there.ROOM: We were on the top floor with a corner suite and it was fantastic. We had the view between the two adjacent hotels but could see the beach and the ocaen. Every morning we got up and went out on the lanai and watched the surfers and just enjoyed the weather; BEAUTIFUL. We were also able to see the fireworks that occur every Friday night at the Hilton; what a treat for our family. The room was plenty big, the beds were very comfortable, and the bath big enough for two people to get ready at the same time. There is an inroom safe as well. BREAKFAST: Every morning there is a buffet but you can't get soda out of the machine. There was always someone there playing some sort of Hawaiian music which created a really relaxing atmosphere. In additon to the usual breakfast foods at Embassy they also offered fresh fruit and rice and linguica. I had read that some people were wondering what the crowds would be like if the hotel was full; the hotel was at 95% and there was never a problem getting a seat at breakfast or in the evening.EVENING RECEPTION: Every night from 5:30 to 7:30; the snacks could improve as they were always the same and after 8 days it got kind of boring. They were chips and salsa, goldfish, some sort of lemon pepper potato chips, and chex mix. The drinks are free but on some nights you could only get one at a time; so if you needed one for your significant other you had to wait in line again. There was always music and a hula dancer except for the night they had a local duet that was having a CD release party which was quite fun for our children.ACTIVITIES: Of note, the two activities desks located within the hotel, one is where you would expect the concierge to be, is a commissioned sales desk. They are trying to sell you any package they can; buyer beware. They sold us a luau at Paradise Cove which was terrrible and I will review under that heading. We did try and make reservations for next year during our stay but were told we had to wait until at least July; not sure why and no one could explain why we had to wait.The Beachwalk area is beautiful and very impressive at night with the torches at street level lit and all aglow. If you want to eat at the Yardhouse get there early or plan to wait a while; it is very busy.SHOPPING: We walked all around inlcuding going to the International Maket Place, Hilo Hattties, and the Ala Moana mall. There is also a street maket every Thursday night (maybe Friday)iwithin walking distance which was fun.The International Market Place is like going to another country. I found it to an experience I don't need to do again. It was quite overwhelming for our children, as well as, if you didn't want to buy what they had for sale they took exception to it. It was a feeling of, if you don't buy it, don't touch it. I did find that most souveniers you could get at the International Market Place, you could get right across the street from Embassy at the ABC store.The Ala Moana mall was quite impressive with all the high end stores you would want. At the mall they have some really good chain restaurants to eat at that weren't any more expensive than they are on the mainland.We took the free shuttle to Hilo Hatties as most of the magazines with discount coupons in them have a three and four page color ad for this place listing it as the place to shop. If your kids would enoy the Trolley ride then go; if not then don't bother, it was a huge waste of time. They tell you that if you get off at the mall to go shopping that they will take you back into Waikiki; don't believe them. We stood there for 20 mintues waiting for the Trolley only to have it go zipping by us at 40 mph and not even slow down. We wound up paying to take the city bus back. Enjoy!!!!!

<Author>BL24
<Content>Get in before Trump steals the view! My wife and I stayed here in early May and our expectations were exceeded. There's always a lot to be said when a hotel is almost brand new so that aspect certainly weighs in heavily. Friendly service upon check-in and very nice bellstaff. We were upgraded to a corner ocean view room. Our room had 2 lanais so we could see the city, pool, and harbor on one side and the ocean on the other. Rooms are spacious and include flat panel TVs, great beds, and attractive furnishings. The one drawback of this hotel, as nearly everyone else mentions, is the Trump Tower going up next door. It is going to take over almost all of the great views from the Embassy Suites. Currently, they're laying the foundation which resulted in a lot of construction noise. This was especially distracting when lounging by the pool as the pool is almost on top of the construction site. The pool area is great though- lots of lounge chairs and the pool itself was larger than most others in the Waikiki area. The manager's reception was great- free cocktails and a terrific Hawaiian band with a hula dancer. Great access to the new Beachwalk area with plenty of great shopping and numerous restaurants. I'd be happy to stay here in the future, but I'm concerned that the views will be non-existent once The Donald gets his development completed next door.

<Content>Nice!!!!! As a Hilton Honors member I always stay at Embassy Suites and/or Hiltons. This property was new and nice. A little noisey during business hours on the west side due to the Trump Towers Construction and drilling of the foundation but we didnt spend much time during the day in the room. The service was great and very helpful as to the local hot spots. The pool guy Jason was very good at getting you to the good beaches and local spots for food and fun. Thanks Jason. He has some good reccomendations for the North Shore in Haleiwa, such as the Grass Skirt Grill (Big plate of fish, rice, and salad for $11.00) Matsumoto Shaved Ice, and all the surf shops were very cool and friendly. The Shark Cove Grill located in a trailer near Sunset Beach was very good despite the looks of the trailer. Good food!!For a rental car check the internet rather than purchase at the hotel. We saved almost $30 a day by checking the internet at the hotel. Parking is $25 a day but you have no choice in Wakiki. The parking guys were great. The Yard House Rest is just below the hotel and great food, fun, and the bar is happening. We were refered to a sushi Rest at the Hyatt in Honolulu named Musashi. (Located inside the the Hyatt building 3rd floor)GREAT FOOD AND SERVICE AND VERY RESPONABLE!! I would go back again if in town. It was not busy on our Friday night dinner...The Ocean Bird Rest is about 100 yards from the E.S. and good nightly music and drinks. Have a seat on the beach and have a drink and watch and listen the waves. NICE way to impress your sig other. Check out the Swap Meet at the stadium on Wed's. Great deals on Hawaiin shirts, gifts, jewerly, used boogie boards, and just everything Hawaiin. Well worth the trip. Saved a bunch on gifts for friends.

<Author>beachedwhale8
<Content>Great price for families, but a little noisy The two bedroom suite was clean and roomy. The staff was friendly. It is a smaller hotel, so the service is more personal and faster than the Hilton Hawaiian. Valet parking was very quick, I never waited more than a couple of minutes. Lots of good restaurants in area, we enjoyed dining at the YardHouse.Roy's was not open yet. The free breakfast was better than I expected, not as good as the $25 breakfast buffet at the Hilton but close enough. The business center was useful for printing boarding passes, also free internet access in the rooms. The area is noisy from construction, it will be much noiser when the Trump starts building. The beach was one block away, but it was quite rocky in the closest access point. The scenery of the grounds is lacking or nonexistent. Overall, I would stay here again. My family of five would need to rent two rooms in any other hotel, but a two bedroom suite at the Embassy Suites was cheaper and provided more space.

<Content>It was okay Prior reviews mentioned there was quite a bit ofconstruction going on around the hotel..sidewalks, streets, etc.Trump has not started building...I think the noise levelwould be very loud..especially in the drive through lobbyarea. There isn't much of a lobby..it's quite small...you aregreeted by a friendly staff who offer fresh juice while you getchecked in. Valet parking is $25/day...there are no other options.The last night we were there we had to wait almost 20 minutesfor the valet guy to retrieve our car because too many cars werecoming into their driveway at the same time people were tryingto get their cars to leave the hotel. It was a monumental trafficmess of 3 lanes of cars in that lobby area. I'm guessing whenthe hotel is full, it will be a BIG problem.The newer Aloha tower opened..we stayed in the Hula tower.Free internet access is available on the 3rd floor of theAloha tower.We stayed on the 19th floor...with a slight view of the ocean...when you peek out on the lanai. We didn't hearmuch noise from the street level..however, you certainlycan hear people chatting in nearby rooms eitherabove, below, or next door to you.The best rooms were at the end of the floor...rooms 1929 and1930 as they had lanai's that face the ocean.As mentioned in the prior reviews, the room was smallerthan other Embassy Suites rooms that I've stayed in..nocloset...had an armoire.. The rooms were kept clean, andtowels were changed daily...the housekeeping staff werefriendly.I felt the bedroom (2 Q beds) was alittle cramped. Both rooms had flat screen TV's. The living room had a sofa bed..anda table with 4 chairs. Entry into the room you would viewa bar area that had a mini sink, microwave oven, andmini refrigerator.Each room receives a freebie daily newspaper.The free buffet breakfast was basically standard fare ofscrambled eggs, bacon, fresh fruit, sausages, bagels,toast, cereal, cooked to ordered omelette....coffee, juice,milk, etc. At times, we had a singer entertain us..otherwise,it was a wide screen TV.The mgr's reception at 5:30 PM - 7:30 PM.. offered sodas, wine, drinks...nomixed drinks available (ie..no mai tai's, pina coladas..as theydidn't have a blender available). The snacks consistedof chips, salsa, and a Pepperidge Farm snack mix..that's it...nothing excited. I went to one reception..and a great trioof Hawaiian singers were entertaining us. You need toshow your room key to order drinks.The breakfast and mgr's reception was held on the 4thfloor area near the pool. The pool is small with lots ofchaise chairs. I think if you wouldn't appreciate alot of noise...it probably wouldbe a good idea to stay above the 10th floor or higher...Parts of of side lobby area was still under construction..painting...etc. Most of the Beachwalk shops were open...there is anescalor access from the street to the 4th floor of the hotel.You must use your key to use the elevator and to gainentrance to your roomThe hotel was very close to the shopping areas...onKalakua...lots of shopping centers. The Royal HawaiianShopping center is being revamped..and only part of itis open..the end that is closest to Beachwalk...by ourhotel.Beachwalk is a ONE way narrow street coming off ofKalakua.Overall, I think it was nice staying in a new hotel..roomswere slightly smaller than I would have liked, but they wereclean and close to the Waikiki shopping areas andbeaches. Pricewise, it's on par with other major hotelsin the area.Something to think about:.. when this hotel is FULLY booked, howwill they deal with having enough tables/seats for all theguests during breakfast, mgr's reception, and dealing withalot of cars coming in  out of the valet parking area/lobby...noise will be a major concern when Trump starts buildinghis condo/hotel next door.
